B.--Stone inscriptions copied in 1909 (continued from last Annual Report).


ARIE/1910-1911/B/1909/106 (page 16)
Placement
On the west wall of the Kāśī Vīśva-nātha temple at Komaraliṅgam.
Dynasty
…
King
Tribhuvanachakravartin [Vī]rarajēn-dradēva, ‘who was pleased to rule the two Koṅgus together’
Date
20th year
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Beginning lost. Gift of money by Śōḻaṉ Laṅkēśvaradēva to the temple of Tiruvālandurai-Uḍaiyār at Tiruvālandurai in Karaivaḻi-nāḍu, for the decoration (mēlpūchchu) of the idol.

Tribhuvanachakravartin Kōṉēriṉmai-koṇḍāṉ Vīrarājēndradēva.

25th year and Śaka 1153.
Language
Grantha & Tamil
Remarks
Gift of land for offerings to the 10 Āḻvārs in the temple of Aḻagar at Tiru-māliruñjōlai in Kīḻ-Iraṇiyamuṭṭa-nāḍu, sub-division of Pāṇḍi-maṇḍalam. The land was situated in the village of Ulaguḍaiyapirāṭṭi-chaturvēdimaṅ-galam in Rājarāja-vaḷanāḍu which was split up from Karaivaḻi-nāḍu.

Kōnērmaikoṇḍāṉ
Date
…
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Records that the king caused a linga to be set up, and a temple to be built on the occasion of a solar eclipse which happened on the day of his janma-nakshatra (i.e. the star of his nativity) and called it Vīra-Chōḷīśvara.

ARIE/1910-1911/B/1909/150 (page 18)
Placement
Do.
Dynasty
…
King
Parakēsarivarman alias Tribhuvana-chakravartin Vīra Chōḷadēva, “who ruled the two Koṅgus together.”
Date
21st year
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Gift of land for offerings to the temple of Vīraśōḻa-Isvaram-Uḍaiyār set up by the king for his merit at Koḻumam in Karaivaḻi-nāḍu. Another incom-plete record on the same wall, of Vira-Chōḷa, “who ruled the two Koṅgus together” refers to founding of the temple and attempts to give a list of the lands presented to it on the occasion. Still another record gives the 23rd year of, apparently, the same king and mentions Vīraśōḻan-tirumaḍai-viḷāgam.

Kōṉērimēnkoṇḍāṉ

Bahudhānya.
Language
Tamil
Remarks
In modern characters. Gift of land in Tiribuvanamādēviviḷāgam near Kūvam, to a temple whose name is doubtful.
ARIE/1910-1911/B/1909/328 (page 28)
Placement
On the north and west walls of the same shrine.
Dynasty
Chōḷa
King
Parakēsarivarman alias Uḍaiyār śrī-Rājēndradēva.
Date
5th year
Language
Tamil
Remarks
Sale of land by the assembly of Kōṭṭūr alias Chōḷavidyādhara-chaturvēdi-maṅgalam, through which a feeder-channel to the Tiribuvanamādēvip-periyēri at Kūvam alias Madhurāntakanallur, was to pass.

This land was presented to the temple by the purchaser in the 20th year of Chakravartin Kulōttuṇga-Chōḷadēva.

On a slab set up in front of the Añjanēya temple at Jūlakallu.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 1699, Hēv[i] ḻambi.
Language
Telugu
Remarks
Records the reconsecration of the Āñjanēya temple at Juvvulakallu in Bellaṁ-koṇḍa-śīma during the rule of Mallarāju Guṇḍārāyaṇiṅgāru and a gift of land to it for offerings. Another slab in the same place records that twelve years later the temples of Gōpālasvāmin and Bhīmēśvara at Juvvulakallu were repaired and reconsecrated.

ARIE/1910-1911/B/1909/554 (page 42)
Placement
On a slab set up in the courtyard of the Chennakēśvarasvāmiṅ temple in the same village.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 1547, Raktākshi
Language
Telugu
Remarks
Records that the temple of Chennakēśavasvāmi which was formerly built by the heroes (vīrulavāru) in the town of Kāreṁpūṇḍi alias Uddaṇḍavīra-Tirupatī in Vilāyati-kasubā (?), had become dilapidated and the image of the god mutilated. A servant of Aḍsumballi Rāmānāyaniṅgāru renovated the temple and the images, together with those of the Āḷvārs and made grants of land for offerings.
ARIE/1910-1911/B/1909/555 (page 42)
Placement
On a beam of the tower called Nāyuḍu-maṇḍapa in the middle of the same village.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 1367, Raktākshi.
Language
Telugu
Remarks
Records the erection of the tower (mēḍa) by Jīvaraksha Timana, son of Mācherla Chennuḍu at the spot where Chilama Nāyuḍu, planted his spear. Pinamallidēvarāju, Chilama Nāyuḍu, Jīvaraksha Timanā, Peda-mallidēvarāju, Vōbinēni and his wife, his brother Mācherla Timana and the latter's son, are all figured on the beam, some holding spears and others standing in a worshipping posture.

Remarks
Mentions the 15th year of Rājēndra-Chōḷadēva in which the goddess Umā-Paramēśvarī was set up and registers a gift of land to it by the assembly of Madhurāntaka-chaturvēdimaṅgalam. In continuation of this inscription is another, dated in the 15th year of a king whose name is doubtful. It records a gift of land to the shrine of the same goddess by the residents of A bar-nagara.
